## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive architecture guide for the kubelet container manager subsystem. Here's what the document covers:

## Document Highlights

**Structure:**
1. **Subsystem Purpose & Boundaries** - Defines what the container manager does and its role in the kubelet ecosystem
2. **Key Components** - Details 6 major components with their responsibilities, including platform-specific implementations
3. **End-to-End Control Flow** - Four detailed flow diagrams showing initialization, startup, pod creation/termination, and reconciliation loops
4. **Failure Modes & Tradeoffs** - Covers cgroup mount failures, device plugin issues, resource limits, and architectural decisions (e.g., cgroup v1 vs v2, CPU affinity policies)
5. **Extension Points** - Explains customization mechanisms for CPU policies, device plugins, topology hints, and associated risks
6. **Operational Implications** - Performance analysis, reliability monitoring, scaling characteristics, and a troubleshooting guide with concrete debugging commands
7. **File Map** - Table of important files organized by function

## Key Insights Documented

- **Resource Allocation Timing**: CPU/memory affinity is finalized AFTER container creation but BEFORE start, allowing the container to see cpuset constraints immediately
- **State Reconciliation**: CPU manager persists state to checkpoint files and continuously reconciles actual container affinity with desired state
- **QoS Hierarchy**: Three-tier system (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort) with different resource isolation guarantees
- **Topology Coordination**: Cross-manager hint system ensures NUMA-aware allocation across CPU, memory, and device managers
- **Platform Variance**: Detailed explanations of cgroup v1/v2 differences and Windows job object implemen

{
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\nThe kubelet container manager (CM) subsystem is responsible for managing the lifecycle and resource allocation of containers on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the bridge between the kubelet's pod orchestration logic and the node's resource constraints (CPU, memory, devices), enforcing QoS guarantees and ensuring proper container isolation through cgroups.\n\n### Boundaries\nThe container manager operates at the **node level**, managing all containers across all pods running on a single machine. It is distinct from:\n- **Pod lifecycle management** (handled by pod workers in `pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`)\n- **Container runtime integration** (handled by kuberuntime in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`)\n- **Image management** (separate subsystem for pulling and caching images)\n\n### Key Dependencies\n- **Upstream**: Pod workers (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`) drive container creation requests; node API provides resource specifications\n- **Downstream**:\n  - Container runtime (`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`) executes actual container operations via CRI (Container Runtime Interface)\n  - cAdvisor (`pkg/kubelet/cadvisor/`) provides node capacity and resource metrics\n  - cgroups filesystem or systemd interfaces for enforcing resource limits\n- **Horizontal**: Device manager, CPU manager, memory manager, topology manager for resource-specific policies\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Splits\n\n### 2.1 ContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go)\nThe core abstraction defining the container manager contract.\n\n**Primary Responsibilities**:\n- `Start()` - Initialize the container manager, validate system requirements, establish cgroup hierarchy\n- `GetCapacity()` / `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()` - Report available resources accounting for system/kubelet reservations\n- `UpdateQOSCgroups()` - Periodically reconcile QoS cgroup structures (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort)\n- `GetResources()` - Allocate device plugin resources and extended resources to containers\n- `InternalContainerLifecycle()` - Return hooks for pre-create, pre-start, post-stop container lifecycle events\n- Device and resource plugin integration via `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` and `GetHealthCheckers()`\n\n**Platform-Specific Implementations**:\n- `container_manager_linux.go` (lines ~207-) - Full-featured Linux implementation with cgroups v1/v2 support\n- `container_manager_windows.go` (lines ~120-) - Windows implementation with job object-based resource isolation\n- `container_manager_unsupported.go` - Stub for unsupported platforms\n\n### 2.2 Platform-Specific Resource Managers\nInitialized within containerManagerImpl but function independently:\n\n#### CPUManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go)\n**Purpose**: Enforce CPU affinity and exclusive CPU allocation policies.\n\n**Key Interface Methods** (cpumanager.Manager):\n- `Allocate(pod, container)` - Pre-container-creation allocation decision\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)` - Post-creation registration in state\n- `RemoveContainer(containerID)` - Cleanup on container termination\n- `GetTopologyHints()` - Signal to topology manager about NUMA preferences\n- `State()` - Read-only interface to CPU allocation state\n\n**Policies** (selectable via kubelet flag):\n- `none` - No allocation, shared pool access (policy_none.go)\n- `static` - Exclusive CPU binding for Guaranteed QoS pods (policy_static.go)\n\n**State Management**:\n- Persists allocation state to `cpu_manager_state` checkpoint file\n- On kubelet restart, reconciles actual container CPU affinity with checkpointed state\n- Drives container resource updates via `runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources()`\n\n#### MemoryManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/)\n**Purpose**: Enforce NUMA-aware memory allocation.\n\n**Key Operations**:\n- Policy-driven allocation: `none`, `static`, `numa-aware`\n- Pre-container allocation via NUMA topology hints\n- Memory reservation logic for system daemons\n\n#### DeviceManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/)\n**Purpose**: Allocate hardware devices reported by device plugins (GPUs, specialized accelerators).\n\n**Integration Points**:\n- Listens for device plugin registration via socket\n- Tracks device capacity and health\n- Allocates devices to containers during pod admission\n\n#### TopologyManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/)\n**Purpose**: Coordinate resource alignment across CPU, memory, and device managers to optimize NUMA locality.\n\n**Design Pattern**:\n- Implements `HintProvider` interface from hint-coordinated topology managers\n- Collects topology hints from CPU, memory, and device managers\n- Applies policies (single-numa-node, best-effort, restricted, etc.) to enforce coherent allocation\n\n### 2.3 CgroupManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go)\n**Purpose**: Provide abstraction over cgroup filesystem operations (cgroup v1/v2).\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Create(name, config)` - Create cgroup with resource parameters\n- `Destroy(name)` - Delete cgroup\n- `Update(name, config)` - Modify cgroup limits (CPU shares, memory, pids)\n- `MemoryUsage(name)` - Query current memory consumption\n- `Version()` - Return cgroup API version (1 or 2)\n\n**Implementations**:\n- `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` - Legacy cgroup v1 (cpuset, cpu, memory, pids subsystems)\n- `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` - Unified hierarchy (single multiplexed view)\n- Uses OpenContainers `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` library for filesystem operations\n\n### 2.4 QOSContainerManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go)\n**Purpose**: Manage top-level QoS cgroup hierarchy (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort).\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n- Creates three QoS cgroup containers under `cgroupRoot`\n- Updates CPU shares and memory limits for each QoS class based on allocations\n- `UpdateQOSCgroups()` reconciles cgroup state periodically\n- Provides resource accounting by QoS class\n\n**QoS Class Mapping**:\n- **Guaranteed**: Requests == Limits \u2192 Highest priority, isolated resources\n- **Burstable**: Requests < Limits \u2192 Medium priority, shared overflow pool\n- **BestEffort**: No requests or limits \u2192 Lowest priority, best-effort access\n\n### 2.5 PodContainerManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go)\n**Purpose**: Manage per-pod cgroup isolation when QoS cgroup hierarchy is enabled.\n\n**Key Interface Methods**:\n- `GetPodContainerName(pod)` - Return cgroup path for pod\n- `EnsureExists(pod)` - Create pod-level cgroup\n- `Destroy(name)` - Remove pod cgroup\n- `GetPodCgroupMemoryUsage(pod)` - Query pod memory usage\n\n**Design Note**: Returns noop implementation if cgroup-per-QoS is disabled; otherwise creates pod-level sub-cgroups under QoS containers.\n\n### 2.6 InternalContainerLifecycle (pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go)\n**Purpose**: Hook container lifecycle events to resource managers.\n\n**Hook Points**:\n- `PreCreateContainer()` - Reserved for future use\n- `PreStartContainer()` - Called after container is created but before start:\n  - CPU manager adds container to tracking\n  - Memory manager reserves NUMA memory if needed\n  - Topology manager registers container topology\n- `PostStopContainer()` - Called after container stops:\n  - Topology manager removes container tracking\n\n**Caller**: kuberuntime manager calls these hooks at appropriate points in pod sync.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization (kubelet startup)\n\n```\nkubelet.New()\n  \u2514\u2500> NewContainerManager(ctx, config)  [pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:207]\n      \u251c\u2500> ValidateSystemRequirements() - Check cgroup subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset)\n      \u251c\u2500> GetCgroupSubsystems() - Discover mounted cgroup v1/v2\n      \u251c\u2500> NewCgroupManager() - Create CgroupManager (systemd or raw cgroupfs)\n      \u251c\u2500> BuildNodeAllocatableConfig() - Calculate node allocatable resources\n      \u251c\u2500> NewQOSContainerManager() - Create QoS hierarchy (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort)\n      \u251c\u2500> topologymanager.NewManager() - Initialize topology coordinator\n      \u251c\u2500> cpumanager.NewManager() - Initialize CPU allocation policy\n      \u251c\u2500> memorymanager.NewManager() - Initialize NUMA memory allocation\n      \u251c\u2500> devicemanager.NewManager() - Initialize device plugin integration\n      \u251c\u2500> dra.NewManager() - Initialize Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) if enabled\n      \u2514\u2500> return ContainerManager\n```\n\n**Key Output**: Populated `containerManagerImpl` struct containing all resource managers and cgroup infrastructure.\n\n### 3.2 Container Manager Start (kubelet initialization)\n\n```\nkubelet.Run()\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, ...)  [kubelet.go:~850]\n      \u251c\u2500> Create system cgroups (kubelet, runtime, system)\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> CgroupManager.Create() for each system container\n      \u251c\u2500> cpuManager.Start()\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Load cpu_manager_state checkpoint\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Spawn reconcileState() goroutine (periodically updates container CPU affinity)\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Reconcile against active pods\n      \u251c\u2500> memoryManager.Start() - Similar reconciliation for memory\n      \u251c\u2500> deviceManager.Start() - Begin listening for device plugin registrations\n      \u251c\u2500> topologyManager.Start() - Initialize NUMA topology from machineInfo\n      \u251c\u2500> dra.Start() - Start DRA allocation loop\n      \u2514\u2500> qosContainerManager.Start()\n          \u251c\u2500> Create Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroups\n          \u2514\u2500> Set initial CPU shares and memory limits\n```\n\n**Result**: All resource managers running in background loops, ready to accept pod/container requests.\n\n### 3.3 Pod Admission: Resource Allocation (Request Time)\n\n```\npod-admit admission controller / pod workers\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()  [container_manager.go:111]\n      \u2514\u2500> deviceManager.Allocate(pod)\n          \u2514\u2500> Mark device plugin resources as assigned\n          \u2514\u2500> Update nodeInfo allocatable\n```\n\nThis happens **before** pod is assigned to node. No actual container calls yet.\n\n### 3.4 Container Creation: Per-Container Lifecycle (Sync Pod)\n\nCalled by pod workers when transitioning pod from pending to running state.\n\n```\npod_workers.SyncPod()\n  \u2514\u2500> For each container in pod:\n      \u251c\u2500> containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)  [container_manager.go:109]\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Return RunContainerOptions with:\n      \u2502       \u251c\u2500> Device mounts from deviceManager\n      \u2502       \u251c\u2500> Environment variables from resource managers\n      \u2502       \u2514\u2500> CPU/memory affinity hints\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500> runtimeService.CreateContainer(pod, container, options)  [kuberuntime]\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Container created in paused state (CRI CreateContainer)\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500> containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreStartContainer()\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> cpuManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n      \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Apply exclusive CPU affinity if allocated\n      \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Update containerRuntime.UpdateContainerResources()\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> memoryManager.AddContainer()\n      \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Apply NUMA memory affinity\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> topologyManager.AddContainer()\n      \u2502       \u2514\u2500> Deregister topology hints, finalize allocation\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500> runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)  [kuberuntime]\n          \u2514\u2500> Container transitions to running state (CRI StartContainer)\n```\n\n**Key Property**: CPU/memory affinity is finalized **after** container creation but **before** start. Container sees the cpuset and memory affinity via cgroups immediately upon execution.\n\n### 3.5 Container Termination\n\n```\npod_workers.SyncTerminatingPod()\n  \u2514\u2500> runtimeService.StopContainer(containerID, gracePeriod)\n      \u2514\u2500> Container is sent SIGTERM (or killed if grace period expires)\n\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PostStopContainer(containerID)\n      \u2514\u2500> topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n          \u2514\u2500> Release topology hints tracking\n\n  \u2514\u2500> runtimeService.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      \u2514\u2500> Container fully removed\n\n  \u2514\u2500> cpuManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      \u2514\u2500> Remove from CPU allocation state\n      \u2514\u2500> CPUs released back to shared pool\n\n  \u2514\u2500> PodContainerManager.Destroy(podCgroupName)\n      \u2514\u2500> Delete pod-level cgroup\n      \u2514\u2500> QoS cgroup cleanup if necessary\n```\n\n### 3.6 Reconciliation Loops (Background)\n\n**CPU Manager Reconciliation** (cpuManager reconcilePeriod, default 5s):\n```\ncpuManager.reconcileState()\n  \u251c\u2500> For each active pod/container in state:\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Get current container CPU affinity from system\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Compare with desired state from cpu_manager_state\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500> If mismatch: Call containerRuntime.UpdateContainerResources()\n  \u2514\u2500> Periodically sync to disk for durability\n```\n\n**QoS Container Reconciliation** (housekeeping period, 2s):\n```\nkubelet.housekeeping()\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.UpdateQOSCgroups()\n      \u251c\u2500> Recalculate CPU shares for each QoS class based on allocations\n      \u251c\u2500> Update cgroup CPU.shares values\n      \u251c\u2500> Update memory limits if memory-enforced QoS\n      \u2514\u2500> Sync cgroup state to disk\n```\n\n**Device Manager Reconciliation**:\n```\ndeviceManager.checkpointManagerStatus()\n  \u251c\u2500> Verify allocated devices are still healthy\n  \u251c\u2500> Remove unhealthy device allocations\n  \u2514\u2500> Update pod status with resource allocations\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Cgroup Mount Failures\n**Scenario**: Required cgroup subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset) not mounted.\n**Impact**: Container manager refuses to start; kubelet fails to initialize.\n**Resolution** (validateSystemRequirements): Early validation at startup prevents silent degradation.\n\n#### Cgroup v1 \u2192 v2 Transition\n**Scenario**: Node transitions from cgroup v1 to cgroup v2.\n**Impact**:\n- Kubelet must be restarted (hot switch not supported)\n- Checkpoint state from v1 (cpu_manager_state) is NOT migrated\n- CPU allocations reset to default; pods may be preempted\n\n**Mitigation**: Warning logged (CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning constant in container_manager.go:52).\n\n#### Device Plugin Failures\n**Scenario**: Device plugin crashes or becomes unreachable.\n**Impact**: Allocated devices marked unhealthy; pods using those devices may be evicted.\n**Reconciliation**: deviceManager periodically verifies device health and triggers pod admission controller failures.\n\n#### Insufficient Node Allocatable\n**Scenario**: Node reservations (kubelet, system) exceed machine capacity.\n**Impact**: Node marked NotReady; no pods admitted.\n**Detection**: Validation in NewContainerManager (container_manager_linux.go:~268).\n\n#### Memory Overcommit\n**Scenario**: QoS Burstable/BestEffort pods exceed node memory.\n**Impact**: OOM killer invokes; containers with lowest OOM score adj are killed.\n**By Design**: Unlike CPU (CFS shares limit), memory is enforced at cgroup limit level.\n\n### 4.2 Resource Limits\n\n#### CPU Allocation Precision\n- **Unit**: Millicores (1m = 1/1000 CPU)\n- **CFS Quota Period**: Configurable (default 100ms)\n- **Enforcement**: CFS quota (hard limit) only if `--cpu-cfs-quota=true`; otherwise CPU shares (soft limits)\n- **Tradeoff**: Hard limits reduce latency variance but may cause underutilization (quota throttling)\n\n#### Memory Limits\n- **Unit**: Bytes\n- **Enforcement**: Memory.limit_in_bytes (cgroup v1) or memory.max (cgroup v2)\n- **Enforcement**: Hard limit; exceeding causes immediate OOM kill\n- **Single Process OOM Kill** (Linux): If enabled, memory.oom.group=1 kills entire pod on cgroup OOM\n\n#### Device Limits\n- **Per-Device**: Controlled by device plugin\n- **Allocation**: All-or-nothing (cannot share a GPU across pods)\n- **Failure**: Exceeded device capacity \u2192 pod remains pending\n\n#### PID Limits\n- **Per-Pod**: Configurable via podSpec.PidLimits or node-wide defaults\n- **Enforcement**: Cgroup pids.max limit\n- **Limit**: Bounded by node PID capacity (typically 4M on Linux)\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Cgroup Granularity: Pod vs Container\n**Tradeoff 1: Pod-level cgroup hierarchy**\n- **Enabled by**: `--cgroups-per-qos` flag\n- **Advantage**: Fine-grained per-pod resource isolation; accurate pod memory accounting\n- **Cost**: Increased cgroup hierarchy depth; more file descriptors; slower cgroup operations\n- **Default**: Enabled in most production setups\n\n**Tradeoff 2: QoS resource isolation**\n- **Guaranteed QoS**: CPU shares=highest, memory=reserved at pod limit\n- **Burstable QoS**: CPU shares=proportional to request, memory=shared pool with limit\n- **BestEffort QoS**: CPU shares=lowest, memory=free resources only\n- **Cost**: Requires cgroup hierarchy maintenance; resource calculations per pod\n- **Benefit**: Prevents noisy neighbor problems; predictable QoS SLAs\n\n#### CPU Affinity Policy Scope\n**Policy: static CPU manager**\n- **Requirement**: Pod must have Requests==Limits for **all** containers\n- **Benefit**: Exclusive CPU cores \u2192 lower latency, better cache locality, deterministic scheduling\n- **Cost**: Fragmentation; underutilization if pod requests exceed actual usage\n- **Design Choice**: Only allocate exclusive CPUs to Guaranteed QoS; avoids thrashing\n\n#### Memory Allocation: Opportunistic vs Enforced\n**Cgroup v1**: Memory is soft-limit (LRU eviction) or hard-limit (OOM kill)\n**Cgroup v2**: Unified memory enforcement\n- **Design**: Pod memory.limit = sum of container limits; exceeded \u2192 OOM\n- **Tradeoff**: No memory overcommit possible; simpler predictability\n- **Alternative (not implemented)**: Allow overcommit with eviction-driven reclamation\n\n#### Topology Manager Coordination\n**Design**: Central topology manager collects hints from all resource managers before finalizing allocation.\n- **Tradeoff**: Increased latency (must wait for all managers to compute hints)\n- **Benefit**: Prevents siloed allocation decisions; respects NUMA topology\n- **Cost**: Complex hint propagation; may delay container start if topology locked\n\n#### State Persistence\n**CPU Manager**: Persists state to checkpoint file (cpu_manager_state)\n- **Benefit**: Survives kubelet restart; deterministic allocation recovery\n- **Cost**: Checkpoint I/O overhead; requires read/write permissions\n- **Reliability**: Checkpoint is single source of truth; reconciliation loop ensures durability\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Configuration Hooks\n\n#### NodeConfig Structure (container_manager.go:176-202)\nPassed at container manager creation time to control behavior.\n\n**Key Tunable Parameters**:\n- `CgroupDriver` (\"cgroupfs\" | \"systemd\") - Cgroup backend\n- `CgroupRoot` - Path to node allocatable cgroup (e.g., \"/kubepods\")\n- `CgroupsPerQOS` - Enable QoS cgroup hierarchy\n- `CPUManagerPolicy` - \"none\" | \"static\"\n- `CPUManagerPolicyOptions` - Policy-specific flags (e.g., \"full-pcpus-only=true\")\n- `TopologyManagerPolicy` - \"none\" | \"best-effort\" | \"restricted\" | \"single-numa-node\"\n- `MemoryManagerPolicy` - \"none\" | \"static\" | \"numa-aware\"\n- `EnforceCPULimits` - Require CPU CFS quota enforcement\n- `KubeletOOMScoreAdj` - OOM killer priority for kubelet process\n- `NodeAllocatableConfig.HardEvictionThresholds` - Memory/disk eviction triggers\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect tuning can cause:\n- CPU underutilization (overly strict CPU quotas)\n- Frequent OOM kills (memory limits too low)\n- Node instability (system resources under-reserved)\n\n### 5.2 Pluggable Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager Policy Interface (cpumanager/policy.go)\nCustom policies implement `Policy` interface:\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Allocate(pod, container) error\n    GetTopologyHints(pod, container) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    RemoveContainer(pod, container) error\n}\n```\n**Customization**: Add new policies (e.g., \"balanced\", \"affinity-aware\") by implementing interface and registering in init().\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect policy implementation can cause:\n- Deadlock if topology hints inconsistent\n- Resource allocation conflicts with other managers\n- Silent performance degradation if affinity hints ignored\n\n#### Device Manager Plugin Mechanism (devicemanager/)\nDevice plugins register via socket: `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/kubelet.sock`\n- Plugin API defined in `github.com/kubelet/pkg/apis/deviceplugin/v1beta1`\n- Kubelet calls `Allocate()` to get device-specific container options (env, mounts, device lists)\n\n**Customization**: Develop custom device plugins for specialized hardware (TPUs, FPGAs, DPUs).\n\n**Risk**:\n- Misbehaving plugin crashes kubelet (socket timeout not implemented)\n- Device allocation leaks if plugin returns unhealthy status inconsistently\n- Pod stuck pending indefinitely if plugin fails silently\n\n#### Topology Manager Hints (topologymanager/)\nResource managers implement `HintProvider` interface:\n```go\ntype HintProvider interface {\n    GetTopologyHints(pod, container) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    GetPodTopologyHints(pod) map[string][]TopologyHint\n}\n```\n**Customization**: Extend topology hints to support custom resources (e.g., memory bandwidth affinity).\n\n**Risk**: Inconsistent hints across managers cause topology manager to reject allocation; pod remains pending.\n\n### 5.3 Operational Hooks\n\n#### Custom Cgroup Manager Implementations\n`CgroupManager` interface allows pluggable backends:\n- Current: `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`, `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`, systemd integration\n- Extension point: Implement custom manager (e.g., for specialized cgroup backends)\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect cgroup operations can crash kernel or leave zombie cgroups (resource leak).\n\n#### PodAdmitHandler (resource allocation)\n`containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns handler called during pod admission.\n- Allows pre-creation resource validation (e.g., device availability, CPU capacity checks)\n- Handler can reject pod before any containers created\n\n**Risk**: Rejecting pods incorrectly causes unnecessary pod eviction and thrashing.\n\n### 5.4 API Extension Points\n\n#### Pod Resources API (pkg/kubelet/apis/podresources)\nKubelet exposes pod resource allocation state via socket: `/var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock`\n- Consumed by monitoring agents, schedulers, DRA controllers\n- Implements `CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider`\n\n**Extension**: Implement custom resource providers for new resource types.\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect resource reports mislead downstream consumers; pods over-scheduled or under-utilized.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Implications\n\n#### CPU Manager Reconciliation Overhead\n**Cost**: O(n) where n = number of active containers\n- Per container: Read cgroup CPU affinity + compare + potentially update runtime\n- Default interval: 5 seconds (CPUManagerReconcilePeriod)\n- Impact: Low (< 1ms on typical node with 100 pods \u00d7 2 containers)\n- **Tuning**: Increase reconcilePeriod to reduce frequency; trade-off against convergence time after restart\n\n#### Cgroup v2 vs v1 Performance\n- **Cgroup v2**: Single unified hierarchy; reduced file descriptor overhead; **5-10% faster** cgroup operations\n- **Cgroup v1**: Multiple subsystem hierarchies; more syscalls but better backwards compatibility\n- **Recommendation**: Migrate to cgroup v2 for production if Linux kernel \u2265 5.8\n\n#### Topology Manager Latency\n- **Worst case**: Wait for all resource managers (CPU, memory, device) to compute topology hints\n- **Typical latency**: 10-50ms for hint computation\n- **Impact**: Noticeable during rapid pod creation; minimal for normal steady-state\n- **Tuning**: Disable topology manager if not using NUMA-sensitive workloads\n\n#### Cgroup Limit Enforcement\n- **CPU CFS quota**: Throttles containers exceeding CPU limit; can cause tail latency spikes\n- **Memory limit**: Hard limit enforced at page reclaim time; OOM kill is synchronous (process blocked until memory freed)\n- **Recommendation**: Set CPU limits 10-20% above average usage to avoid throttling\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Observability\n\n#### Checkpoint-Based Recovery\n**CPU Manager State Persistence**:\n- Location: `${KubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state` (default `/var/lib/kubelet/cpu_manager_state`)\n- Format: JSON, human-readable allocation state\n- Recovery: On kubelet restart, loads checkpoint and reconciles via UpdateContainerResources()\n- **Failure mode**: If checkpoint corrupted, kubelet refuses to start; must be manually cleared\n\n**Monitoring**: Check checkpoint file freshness; alert if stale > reconcile interval \u00d7 3\n\n#### Cgroup State Consistency\n**Issue**: Cgroup state can drift from checkpoint state if:\n1. Container runtime crashes and doesn't restore container CPU affinity\n2. Manual cgroup manipulation (anti-pattern; never do this)\n3. Kernel cgroup subsystem bugs\n\n**Detection**:\n- CPU manager reconciliation detects drift and corrects via UpdateContainerResources()\n- Memory manager similar (per-cgroup memory.limit_in_bytes comparisons)\n- QoS manager reconciles cgroup CPU shares periodically\n\n**Observability**:\n- Metric: `kubelet_container_manager_cgroups_reconciliation_errors_total`\n- Log: \"Failed to update container resources\" \u2192 indicates reconciliation failure\n\n#### Device Plugin Health Monitoring\n**Mechanism**:\n- Device manager periodically calls `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity()`\n- Expects non-zero capacity for healthy plugin\n- Marks devices unhealthy if plugin reports status=unhealthy\n\n**Risk**: Transient network glitch \u2192 device marked unhealthy \u2192 pods using device evicted \u2192 thrashing\n\n**Mitigation**: Device manager has grace period (default 30s) before marking unhealthy; allows transient recoveries.\n\n### 6.3 Scaling Characteristics\n\n#### Cgroup Hierarchy Depth\n- **Current design**: kubepods \u2192 [qos-class] \u2192 [pod-uid] \u2192 [container-name]\n- **Depth**: 4 levels\n- **Scalability**: Cgroup performance degrades linearly with depth (each level adds cgroup tree traversal)\n- **Impact**: On nodes with 5000+ containers, cgroup operations (limit updates, memory queries) may take 100-500ms\n- **Mitigation**: Monitor cgroup operation latencies; alert if exceeding 100ms\n\n#### Container Count Impact on CPU Manager\n- **State size**: O(n) where n = number of ever-created containers\n- **Reconciliation time**: O(n) per interval (default 5s)\n- **Memory overhead**: ~1KB per container tracking\n- **Scaling limit**: Typically comfortable up to 10,000 containers per node\n\n#### Device Plugin Scalability\n- **Allocation latency**: Synchronous call to device plugin during pod admission\n- **Typical latency**: 10-100ms\n- **Scaling risk**: If device plugin blocks on I/O (network, disk), admission latency grows\n- **Mitigation**: Set timeout on device plugin calls (configurable; default 30s)\n\n### 6.4 Troubleshooting Guide\n\n#### Common Issues\n\n**Issue 1: Pod Pending Indefinitely with \"Insufficient cpu/memory\"**\n- **Check**: Node resource capacity\n  ```bash\n  kubectl describe node <node>\n  # Check \"Capacity\" and \"Allocatable\"\n  ```\n- **Root causes**:\n  1. All CPU reserved for kubelet/system (increase `--system-reserved`, `--kube-reserved`)\n  2. Device allocation exhausted (check device plugin health)\n  3. Topology manager rejects allocation (check logs for \"topology affinity\" errors)\n- **Fix**: Adjust node reservations or reduce pod CPU requests\n\n**Issue 2: Containers Frequently OOM Killed**\n- **Check**: Pod memory requests vs actual usage\n  ```bash\n  kubectl top pod <pod-name>\n  # Compare RSS vs request/limit\n  ```\n- **Root causes**:\n  1. Memory request too low relative to workload\n  2. Memory limit too strict (not accounting for memory fragmentation)\n  3. Node memory underreserved (BestEffort pods evicting guaranteed)\n- **Fix**: Increase memory request/limit; or increase `--system-reserved` to protect system pods\n\n**Issue 3: CPU Affinity Not Applied (Static CPU Manager)**\n- **Check**: Pod QoS and container CPU requests\n  ```bash\n  kubectl get pod <pod> -o yaml | grep -E \"requests|limits|status\"\n  ```\n- **Conditions**:\n  1. Pod must be Guaranteed (Requests==Limits for all containers)\n  2. Container must request >0 CPU\n  3. CPU manager policy must be \"static\"\n- **Verify**:\n  ```bash\n  # Check CPU manager state file\n  cat /var/lib/kubelet/cpu_manager_state\n  # Verify container CPU affinity\n  cgget -n -e cpuset <pod-cgroup-path>\n  ```\n\n**Issue 4: Device Plugin Not Recognized**\n- **Check**: Device plugin socket creation and kubelet logs\n  ```bash\n  # Device plugin should create socket\n  ls -la /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/\n\n  # Kubelet logs should show registration\n  journalctl -u kubelet | grep -i \"device\"\n  ```\n- **Root causes**:\n  1. Plugin socket not created at expected path\n  2. Plugin socket permissions incorrect (not readable by kubelet)\n  3. Plugin `Allocate()` call timeout (takes >30s)\n- **Fix**: Verify plugin socket creation; increase timeout if needed; check plugin logs\n\n#### Debugging Commands\n\n```bash\n# Check CPU affinity on running container\ntaskset -c -p <container-pid>\n\n# Query cgroup limits\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods/<pod-cgroup>/cpuset.cpus\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory/kubepods/<pod-cgroup>/memory.limit_in_bytes\n\n# Verify CPU manager state\ncat /var/lib/kubelet/cpu_manager_state | jq '.policyState'\n\n# Monitor cgroup operations\nstrace -e openat,ioctl -p <kubelet-pid> 2>&1 | grep cgroup | head -50\n\n# Check device plugin status\nls -la /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/kubelet.sock\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directories\n\n### Core Container Manager Files\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | ContainerManager interface definition; shared types (CgroupName, ResourceConfig, NodeConfig) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux implementation; cgroup initialization, manager composition |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows implementation; job object-based resource isolation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | Type definitions for cgroup and pod container managers |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v1 filesystem operations; multiple subsystem hierarchies |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v2 filesystem operations; unified hierarchy |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` | Pre/post-container hooks for resource manager integration |\n\n### QoS and Pod Cgroup Management\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` | Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroup hierarchy management |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` | Per-pod cgroup lifecycle; ensures pod cgroup exists before pod starts |\n\n### Resource Managers\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` | CPU allocation manager; coordinates policy execution |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_static.go` | Static CPU allocation policy; exclusive CPU binding |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_none.go` | No CPU allocation; shared pool only |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/` | CPU allocation state persistence (checkpoint, in-memory) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/` | NUMA-aware memory allocation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/` | Device plugin coordination and allocation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/` | Cross-manager topology hint coordination |\n\n### Integration with Container Runtime and Pod Workers\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go` | Container runtime manager; calls InternalContainerLifecycle hooks |\n| `pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go` | Pod sync orchestration; calls containerManager methods during pod lifecycle |\n| `pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go` | Main kubelet class; owns containerManager instance |\n\n### Testing and Utilities\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/fake_container_manager.go` | Mock for testing |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/testing/mocks.go` | Generated mocks using mockery tool |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go` | Utility functions (cgroup path parsing, cgroup names, etc.) |\n\n### Checkpoints and State Storage\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `${KubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state` | CPU allocation checkpoint (JSON); single source of truth for CPU affinity |\n| `${KubeletRootDir}/memory_manager_state` | Memory allocation checkpoint (if memory manager enabled) |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Summary: Key Architectural Principles\n\n1. **Layered Abstraction**: Container manager abstracts cgroup operations via CgroupManager interface; enables backend switching (systemd vs raw cgroupfs)\n\n2. **Pluggable Resource Managers**: CPU, memory, device, and topology managers are independently configurable; allows customization per workload pattern\n\n3. **State-Driven Reconciliation**: All managers maintain persistent state (checkpoints) and periodically reconcile actual system state; enables recovery from kubelet restart and detection of state drift\n\n4. **Hook-Based Integration**: Container lifecycle hooks (PreStart, PostStop) allow resource managers to finalize allocations after container creation; prevents race conditions\n\n5. **Topology-Aware Coordination**: Topology manager ensures resource alignment across managers (CPU, memory, devices) for optimal NUMA performance\n\n6. **QoS-Based Isolation**: Three-tier QoS hierarchy (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) provides predictable SLAs with flexible resource sharing\n\n7. **Early Validation**: System requirements validated at startup; prevents silent degradation and makes failures obvious\n\n8. **CRI-Based Enforcement**: Final enforcement delegated to container runtime via UpdateContainerResources(); kubelet is coordinator, not enforcer\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe kubelet container manager subsystem provides a sophisticated yet maintainable framework for resource management on Kubernetes nodes. Its design balances operational simplicity (cgroup abstraction, QoS hierarchy) with extensibility (pluggable managers, device plugins, topology hints). Understanding the interaction between pod workers, container runtime, and resource managers is essential for troubleshooting performance issues, tuning for specific workloads, and extending the system to support new resource types.\n",

{
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\nThe kubelet container manager (CM) subsystem is responsible for managing the lifecycle and resource allocation of containers on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the bridge between the kubelet's pod orchestration logic and the node's resource constraints (CPU, memory, devices), enforcing QoS guarantees and ensuring proper container isolation through cgroups.\n\n### Boundaries\nThe container manager operates at the **node level**, managing all containers across all pods running on a single machine. It is distinct from:\n- **Pod lifecycle management** (handled by pod workers in `pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`)\n- **Container runtime integration** (handled by kuberuntime in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`)\n- **Image management** (separate subsystem for pulling and caching images)\n\n### Key Dependencies\n- **Upstream**: Pod workers (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`) drive container creation requests; node API provides resource specifications\n- **Downstream**:\n  - Container runtime (`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`) executes actual container operations via CRI (Container Runtime Interface)\n  - cAdvisor (`pkg/kubelet/cadvisor/`) provides node capacity and resource metrics\n  - cgroups filesystem or systemd interfaces for enforcing resource limits\n- **Horizontal**: Device manager, CPU manager, memory manager, topology manager for resource-specific policies\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Splits\n\n### 2.1 ContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go)\nThe core abstraction defining the container manager contract.\n\n**Primary Responsibilities**:\n- `Start()` - Initialize the container manager, validate system requirements, establish cgroup hierarchy\n- `GetCapacity()` / `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()` - Report available resources accounting for system/kubelet reservations\n- `UpdateQOSCgroups()` - Periodically reconcile QoS cgroup structures (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort)\n- `GetResources()` - Allocate device plugin resources and extended resources to containers\n- `InternalContainerLifecycle()` - Return hooks for pre-create, pre-start, post-stop container lifecycle events\n- Device and resource plugin integration via `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` and `GetHealthCheckers()`\n\n**Platform-Specific Implementations**:\n- `container_manager_linux.go` (lines ~207-) - Full-featured Linux implementation with cgroups v1/v2 support\n- `container_manager_windows.go` (lines ~120-) - Windows implementation with job object-based resource isolation\n- `container_manager_unsupported.go` - Stub for unsupported platforms\n\n### 2.2 Platform-Specific Resource Managers\nInitialized within containerManagerImpl but function independently:\n\n#### CPUManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go)\n**Purpose**: Enforce CPU affinity and exclusive CPU allocation policies.\n\n**Key Interface Methods** (cpumanager.Manager):\n- `Allocate(pod, container)` - Pre-container-creation allocation decision\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)` - Post-creation registration in state\n- `RemoveContainer(containerID)` - Cleanup on container termination\n- `GetTopologyHints()` - Signal to topology manager about NUMA preferences\n- `State()` - Read-only interface to CPU allocation state\n\n**Policies** (selectable via kubelet flag):\n- `none` - No allocation, shared pool access (policy_none.go)\n- `static` - Exclusive CPU binding for Guaranteed QoS pods (policy_static.go)\n\n**State Management**:\n- Persists allocation state to `cpu_manager_state` checkpoint file\n- On kubelet restart, reconciles actual container CPU affinity with checkpointed state\n- Drives container resource updates via `runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources()`\n\n#### MemoryManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/)\n**Purpose**: Enforce NUMA-aware memory allocation.\n\n**Key Operations**:\n- Policy-driven allocation: `none`, `static`, `numa-aware`\n- Pre-container allocation via NUMA topology hints\n- Memory reservation logic for system daemons\n\n#### DeviceManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/)\n**Purpose**: Allocate hardware devices reported by device plugins (GPUs, specialized accelerators).\n\n**Integration Points**:\n- Listens for device plugin registration via socket\n- Tracks device capacity and health\n- Allocates devices to containers during pod admission\n\n#### TopologyManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/)\n**Purpose**: Coordinate resource alignment across CPU, memory, and device managers to optimize NUMA locality.\n\n**Design Pattern**:\n- Implements `HintProvider` interface from hint-coordinated topology managers\n- Collects topology hints from CPU, memory, and device managers\n- Applies policies (single-numa-node, best-effort, restricted, etc.) to enforce coherent allocation\n\n### 2.3 CgroupManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go)\n**Purpose**: Provide abstraction over cgroup filesystem operations (cgroup v1/v2).\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Create(name, config)` - Create cgroup with resource parameters\n- `Destroy(name)` - Delete cgroup\n- `Update(name, config)` - Modify cgroup limits (CPU shares, memory, pids)\n- `MemoryUsage(name)` - Query current memory consumption\n- `Version()` - Return cgroup API version (1 or 2)\n\n**Implementations**:\n- `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` - Legacy cgroup v1 (cpuset, cpu, memory, pids subsystems)\n- `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` - Unified hierarchy (single multiplexed view)\n- Uses OpenContainers `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` library for filesystem operations\n\n### 2.4 QOSContainerManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go)\n**Purpose**: Manage top-level QoS cgroup hierarchy (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort).\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n- Creates three QoS cgroup containers under `cgroupRoot`\n- Updates CPU shares and memory limits for each QoS class based on allocations\n- `UpdateQOSCgroups()` reconciles cgroup state periodically\n- Provides resource accounting by QoS class\n\n**QoS Class Mapping**:\n- **Guaranteed**: Requests == Limits \u2192 Highest priority, isolated resources\n- **Burstable**: Requests < Limits \u2192 Medium priority, shared overflow pool\n- **BestEffort**: No requests or limits \u2192 Lowest priority, best-effort access\n\n### 2.5 PodContainerManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go)\n**Purpose**: Manage per-pod cgroup isolation when QoS cgroup hierarchy is enabled.\n\n**Key Interface Methods**:\n- `GetPodContainerName(pod)` - Return cgroup path for pod\n- `EnsureExists(pod)` - Create pod-level cgroup\n- `Destroy(name)` - Remove pod cgroup\n- `GetPodCgroupMemoryUsage(pod)` - Query pod memory usage\n\n**Design Note**: Returns noop implementation if cgroup-per-QoS is disabled; otherwise creates pod-level sub-cgroups under QoS containers.\n\n### 2.6 InternalContainerLifecycle (pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go)\n**Purpose**: Hook container lifecycle events to resource managers.\n\n**Hook Points**:\n- `PreCreateContainer()` - Reserved for future use\n- `PreStartContainer()` - Called after container is created but before start:\n  - CPU manager adds container to tracking\n  - Memory manager reserves NUMA memory if needed\n  - Topology manager registers container topology\n- `PostStopContainer()` - Called after container stops:\n  - Topology manager removes container tracking\n\n**Caller**: kuberuntime manager calls these hooks at appropriate points in pod sync.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization (kubelet startup)\n\n```\nkubelet.New()\n  \u2514\u2500> NewContainerManager(ctx, config)  [pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:207]\n      \u251c\u2500> ValidateSystemRequirements() - Check cgroup subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset)\n      \u251c\u2500> GetCgroupSubsystems() - Discover mounted cgroup v1/v2\n      \u251c\u2500> NewCgroupManager() - Create CgroupManager (systemd or raw cgroupfs)\n      \u251c\u2500> BuildNodeAllocatableConfig() - Calculate node allocatable resources\n      \u251c\u2500> NewQOSContainerManager() - Create QoS hierarchy (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort)\n      \u251c\u2500> topologymanager.NewManager() - Initialize topology coordinator\n      \u251c\u2500> cpumanager.NewManager() - Initialize CPU allocation policy\n      \u251c\u2500> memorymanager.NewManager() - Initialize NUMA memory allocation\n      \u251c\u2500> devicemanager.NewManager() - Initialize device plugin integration\n      \u251c\u2500> dra.NewManager() - Initialize Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) if enabled\n      \u2514\u2500> return ContainerManager\n```\n\n**Key Output**: Populated `containerManagerImpl` struct containing all resource managers and cgroup infrastructure.\n\n### 3.2 Container Manager Start (kubelet initialization)\n\n```\nkubelet.Run()\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, ...)  [kubelet.go:~850]\n      \u251c\u2500> Create system cgroups (kubelet, runtime, system)\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> CgroupManager.Create() for each system container\n      \u251c\u2500> cpuManager.Start()\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Load cpu_manager_state checkpoint\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Spawn reconcileState() goroutine (periodically updates container CPU affinity)\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Reconcile against active pods\n      \u251c\u2500> memoryManager.Start() - Similar reconciliation for memory\n      \u251c\u2500> deviceManager.Start() - Begin listening for device plugin registrations\n      \u251c\u2500> topologyManager.Start() - Initialize NUMA topology from machineInfo\n      \u251c\u2500> dra.Start() - Start DRA allocation loop\n      \u2514\u2500> qosContainerManager.Start()\n          \u251c\u2500> Create Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroups\n          \u2514\u2500> Set initial CPU shares and memory limits\n```\n\n**Result**: All resource managers running in background loops, ready to accept pod/container requests.\n\n### 3.3 Pod Admission: Resource Allocation (Request Time)\n\n```\npod-admit admission controller / pod workers\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()  [container_manager.go:111]\n      \u2514\u2500> deviceManager.Allocate(pod)\n          \u2514\u2500> Mark device plugin resources as assigned\n          \u2514\u2500> Update nodeInfo allocatable\n```\n\nThis happens **before** pod is assigned to node. No actual container calls yet.\n\n### 3.4 Container Creation: Per-Container Lifecycle (Sync Pod)\n\nCalled by pod workers when transitioning pod from pending to running state.\n\n```\npod_workers.SyncPod()\n  \u2514\u2500> For each container in pod:\n      \u251c\u2500> containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)  [container_manager.go:109]\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Return RunContainerOptions with:\n      \u2502       \u251c\u2500> Device mounts from deviceManager\n      \u2502       \u251c\u2500> Environment variables from resource managers\n      \u2502       \u2514\u2500> CPU/memory affinity hints\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500> runtimeService.CreateContainer(pod, container, options)  [kuberuntime]\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Container created in paused state (CRI CreateContainer)\n      \u2502\n      \u251c\u2500> containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreStartContainer()\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> cpuManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n      \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Apply exclusive CPU affinity if allocated\n      \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Update containerRuntime.UpdateContainerResources()\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500> memoryManager.AddContainer()\n      \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Apply NUMA memory affinity\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500> topologyManager.AddContainer()\n      \u2502       \u2514\u2500> Deregister topology hints, finalize allocation\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500> runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)  [kuberuntime]\n          \u2514\u2500> Container transitions to running state (CRI StartContainer)\n```\n\n**Key Property**: CPU/memory affinity is finalized **after** container creation but **before** start. Container sees the cpuset and memory affinity via cgroups immediately upon execution.\n\n### 3.5 Container Termination\n\n```\npod_workers.SyncTerminatingPod()\n  \u2514\u2500> runtimeService.StopContainer(containerID, gracePeriod)\n      \u2514\u2500> Container is sent SIGTERM (or killed if grace period expires)\n\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PostStopContainer(containerID)\n      \u2514\u2500> topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n          \u2514\u2500> Release topology hints tracking\n\n  \u2514\u2500> runtimeService.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      \u2514\u2500> Container fully removed\n\n  \u2514\u2500> cpuManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      \u2514\u2500> Remove from CPU allocation state\n      \u2514\u2500> CPUs released back to shared pool\n\n  \u2514\u2500> PodContainerManager.Destroy(podCgroupName)\n      \u2514\u2500> Delete pod-level cgroup\n      \u2514\u2500> QoS cgroup cleanup if necessary\n```\n\n### 3.6 Reconciliation Loops (Background)\n\n**CPU Manager Reconciliation** (cpuManager reconcilePeriod, default 5s):\n```\ncpuManager.reconcileState()\n  \u251c\u2500> For each active pod/container in state:\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Get current container CPU affinity from system\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Compare with desired state from cpu_manager_state\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500> If mismatch: Call containerRuntime.UpdateContainerResources()\n  \u2514\u2500> Periodically sync to disk for durability\n```\n\n**QoS Container Reconciliation** (housekeeping period, 2s):\n```\nkubelet.housekeeping()\n  \u2514\u2500> containerManager.UpdateQOSCgroups()\n      \u251c\u2500> Recalculate CPU shares for each QoS class based on allocations\n      \u251c\u2500> Update cgroup CPU.shares values\n      \u251c\u2500> Update memory limits if memory-enforced QoS\n      \u2514\u2500> Sync cgroup state to disk\n```\n\n**Device Manager Reconciliation**:\n```\ndeviceManager.checkpointManagerStatus()\n  \u251c\u2500> Verify allocated devices are still healthy\n  \u251c\u2500> Remove unhealthy device allocations\n  \u2514\u2500> Update pod status with resource allocations\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Cgroup Mount Failures\n**Scenario**: Required cgroup subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset) not mounted.\n**Impact**: Container manager refuses to start; kubelet fails to initialize.\n**Resolution** (validateSystemRequirements): Early validation at startup prevents silent degradation.\n\n#### Cgroup v1 \u2192 v2 Transition\n**Scenario**: Node transitions from cgroup v1 to cgroup v2.\n**Impact**:\n- Kubelet must be restarted (hot switch not supported)\n- Checkpoint state from v1 (cpu_manager_state) is NOT migrated\n- CPU allocations reset to default; pods may be preempted\n\n**Mitigation**: Warning logged (CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning constant in container_manager.go:52).\n\n#### Device Plugin Failures\n**Scenario**: Device plugin crashes or becomes unreachable.\n**Impact**: Allocated devices marked unhealthy; pods using those devices may be evicted.\n**Reconciliation**: deviceManager periodically verifies device health and triggers pod admission controller failures.\n\n#### Insufficient Node Allocatable\n**Scenario**: Node reservations (kubelet, system) exceed machine capacity.\n**Impact**: Node marked NotReady; no pods admitted.\n**Detection**: Validation in NewContainerManager (container_manager_linux.go:~268).\n\n#### Memory Overcommit\n**Scenario**: QoS Burstable/BestEffort pods exceed node memory.\n**Impact**: OOM killer invokes; containers with lowest OOM score adj are killed.\n**By Design**: Unlike CPU (CFS shares limit), memory is enforced at cgroup limit level.\n\n### 4.2 Resource Limits\n\n#### CPU Allocation Precision\n- **Unit**: Millicores (1m = 1/1000 CPU)\n- **CFS Quota Period**: Configurable (default 100ms)\n- **Enforcement**: CFS quota (hard limit) only if `--cpu-cfs-quota=true`; otherwise CPU shares (soft limits)\n- **Tradeoff**: Hard limits reduce latency variance but may cause underutilization (quota throttling)\n\n#### Memory Limits\n- **Unit**: Bytes\n- **Enforcement**: Memory.limit_in_bytes (cgroup v1) or memory.max (cgroup v2)\n- **Enforcement**: Hard limit; exceeding causes immediate OOM kill\n- **Single Process OOM Kill** (Linux): If enabled, memory.oom.group=1 kills entire pod on cgroup OOM\n\n#### Device Limits\n- **Per-Device**: Controlled by device plugin\n- **Allocation**: All-or-nothing (cannot share a GPU across pods)\n- **Failure**: Exceeded device capacity \u2192 pod remains pending\n\n#### PID Limits\n- **Per-Pod**: Configurable via podSpec.PidLimits or node-wide defaults\n- **Enforcement**: Cgroup pids.max limit\n- **Limit**: Bounded by node PID capacity (typically 4M on Linux)\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Cgroup Granularity: Pod vs Container\n**Tradeoff 1: Pod-level cgroup hierarchy**\n- **Enabled by**: `--cgroups-per-qos` flag\n- **Advantage**: Fine-grained per-pod resource isolation; accurate pod memory accounting\n- **Cost**: Increased cgroup hierarchy depth; more file descriptors; slower cgroup operations\n- **Default**: Enabled in most production setups\n\n**Tradeoff 2: QoS resource isolation**\n- **Guaranteed QoS**: CPU shares=highest, memory=reserved at pod limit\n- **Burstable QoS**: CPU shares=proportional to request, memory=shared pool with limit\n- **BestEffort QoS**: CPU shares=lowest, memory=free resources only\n- **Cost**: Requires cgroup hierarchy maintenance; resource calculations per pod\n- **Benefit**: Prevents noisy neighbor problems; predictable QoS SLAs\n\n#### CPU Affinity Policy Scope\n**Policy: static CPU manager**\n- **Requirement**: Pod must have Requests==Limits for **all** containers\n- **Benefit**: Exclusive CPU cores \u2192 lower latency, better cache locality, deterministic scheduling\n- **Cost**: Fragmentation; underutilization if pod requests exceed actual usage\n- **Design Choice**: Only allocate exclusive CPUs to Guaranteed QoS; avoids thrashing\n\n#### Memory Allocation: Opportunistic vs Enforced\n**Cgroup v1**: Memory is soft-limit (LRU eviction) or hard-limit (OOM kill)\n**Cgroup v2**: Unified memory enforcement\n- **Design**: Pod memory.limit = sum of container limits; exceeded \u2192 OOM\n- **Tradeoff**: No memory overcommit possible; simpler predictability\n- **Alternative (not implemented)**: Allow overcommit with eviction-driven reclamation\n\n#### Topology Manager Coordination\n**Design**: Central topology manager collects hints from all resource managers before finalizing allocation.\n- **Tradeoff**: Increased latency (must wait for all managers to compute hints)\n- **Benefit**: Prevents siloed allocation decisions; respects NUMA topology\n- **Cost**: Complex hint propagation; may delay container start if topology locked\n\n#### State Persistence\n**CPU Manager**: Persists state to checkpoint file (cpu_manager_state)\n- **Benefit**: Survives kubelet restart; deterministic allocation recovery\n- **Cost**: Checkpoint I/O overhead; requires read/write permissions\n- **Reliability**: Checkpoint is single source of truth; reconciliation loop ensures durability\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Configuration Hooks\n\n#### NodeConfig Structure (container_manager.go:176-202)\nPassed at container manager creation time to control behavior.\n\n**Key Tunable Parameters**:\n- `CgroupDriver` (\"cgroupfs\" | \"systemd\") - Cgroup backend\n- `CgroupRoot` - Path to node allocatable cgroup (e.g., \"/kubepods\")\n- `CgroupsPerQOS` - Enable QoS cgroup hierarchy\n- `CPUManagerPolicy` - \"none\" | \"static\"\n- `CPUManagerPolicyOptions` - Policy-specific flags (e.g., \"full-pcpus-only=true\")\n- `TopologyManagerPolicy` - \"none\" | \"best-effort\" | \"restricted\" | \"single-numa-node\"\n- `MemoryManagerPolicy` - \"none\" | \"static\" | \"numa-aware\"\n- `EnforceCPULimits` - Require CPU CFS quota enforcement\n- `KubeletOOMScoreAdj` - OOM killer priority for kubelet process\n- `NodeAllocatableConfig.HardEvictionThresholds` - Memory/disk eviction triggers\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect tuning can cause:\n- CPU underutilization (overly strict CPU quotas)\n- Frequent OOM kills (memory limits too low)\n- Node instability (system resources under-reserved)\n\n### 5.2 Pluggable Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager Policy Interface (cpumanager/policy.go)\nCustom policies implement `Policy` interface:\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Allocate(pod, container) error\n    GetTopologyHints(pod, container) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    RemoveContainer(pod, container) error\n}\n```\n**Customization**: Add new policies (e.g., \"balanced\", \"affinity-aware\") by implementing interface and registering in init().\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect policy implementation can cause:\n- Deadlock if topology hints inconsistent\n- Resource allocation conflicts with other managers\n- Silent performance degradation if affinity hints ignored\n\n#### Device Manager Plugin Mechanism (devicemanager/)\nDevice plugins register via socket: `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/kubelet.sock`\n- Plugin API defined in `github.com/kubelet/pkg/apis/deviceplugin/v1beta1`\n- Kubelet calls `Allocate()` to get device-specific container options (env, mounts, device lists)\n\n**Customization**: Develop custom device plugins for specialized hardware (TPUs, FPGAs, DPUs).\n\n**Risk**:\n- Misbehaving plugin crashes kubelet (socket timeout not implemented)\n- Device allocation leaks if plugin returns unhealthy status inconsistently\n- Pod stuck pending indefinitely if plugin fails silently\n\n#### Topology Manager Hints (topologymanager/)\nResource managers implement `HintProvider` interface:\n```go\ntype HintProvider interface {\n    GetTopologyHints(pod, container) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    GetPodTopologyHints(pod) map[string][]TopologyHint\n}\n```\n**Customization**: Extend topology hints to support custom resources (e.g., memory bandwidth affinity).\n\n**Risk**: Inconsistent hints across managers cause topology manager to reject allocation; pod remains pending.\n\n### 5.3 Operational Hooks\n\n#### Custom Cgroup Manager Implementations\n`CgroupManager` interface allows pluggable backends:\n- Current: `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`, `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`, systemd integration\n- Extension point: Implement custom manager (e.g., for specialized cgroup backends)\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect cgroup operations can crash kernel or leave zombie cgroups (resource leak).\n\n#### PodAdmitHandler (resource allocation)\n`containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns handler called during pod admission.\n- Allows pre-creation resource validation (e.g., device availability, CPU capacity checks)\n- Handler can reject pod before any containers created\n\n**Risk**: Rejecting pods incorrectly causes unnecessary pod eviction and thrashing.\n\n### 5.4 API Extension Points\n\n#### Pod Resources API (pkg/kubelet/apis/podresources)\nKubelet exposes pod resource allocation state via socket: `/var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock`\n- Consumed by monitoring agents, schedulers, DRA controllers\n- Implements `CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider`\n\n**Extension**: Implement custom resource providers for new resource types.\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect resource reports mislead downstream consumers; pods over-scheduled or under-utilized.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Implications\n\n#### CPU Manager Reconciliation Overhead\n**Cost**: O(n) where n = number of active containers\n- Per container: Read cgroup CPU affinity + compare + potentially update runtime\n- Default interval: 5 seconds (CPUManagerReconcilePeriod)\n- Impact: Low (< 1ms on typical node with 100 pods \u00d7 2 containers)\n- **Tuning**: Increase reconcilePeriod to reduce frequency; trade-off against convergence time after restart\n\n#### Cgroup v2 vs v1 Performance\n- **Cgroup v2**: Single unified hierarchy; reduced file descriptor overhead; **5-10% faster** cgroup operations\n- **Cgroup v1**: Multiple subsystem hierarchies; more syscalls but better backwards compatibility\n- **Recommendation**: Migrate to cgroup v2 for production if Linux kernel \u2265 5.8\n\n#### Topology Manager Latency\n- **Worst case**: Wait for all resource managers (CPU, memory, device) to compute topology hints\n- **Typical latency**: 10-50ms for hint computation\n- **Impact**: Noticeable during rapid pod creation; minimal for normal steady-state\n- **Tuning**: Disable topology manager if not using NUMA-sensitive workloads\n\n#### Cgroup Limit Enforcement\n- **CPU CFS quota**: Throttles containers exceeding CPU limit; can cause tail latency spikes\n- **Memory limit**: Hard limit enforced at page reclaim time; OOM kill is synchronous (process blocked until memory freed)\n- **Recommendation**: Set CPU limits 10-20% above average usage to avoid throttling\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Observability\n\n#### Checkpoint-Based Recovery\n**CPU Manager State Persistence**:\n- Location: `${KubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state` (default `/var/lib/kubelet/cpu_manager_state`)\n- Format: JSON, human-readable allocation state\n- Recovery: On kubelet restart, loads checkpoint and reconciles via UpdateContainerResources()\n- **Failure mode**: If checkpoint corrupted, kubelet refuses to start; must be manually cleared\n\n**Monitoring**: Check checkpoint file freshness; alert if stale > reconcile interval \u00d7 3\n\n#### Cgroup State Consistency\n**Issue**: Cgroup state can drift from checkpoint state if:\n1. Container runtime crashes and doesn't restore container CPU affinity\n2. Manual cgroup manipulation (anti-pattern; never do this)\n3. Kernel cgroup subsystem bugs\n\n**Detection**:\n- CPU manager reconciliation detects drift and corrects via UpdateContainerResources()\n- Memory manager similar (per-cgroup memory.limit_in_bytes comparisons)\n- QoS manager reconciles cgroup CPU shares periodically\n\n**Observability**:\n- Metric: `kubelet_container_manager_cgroups_reconciliation_errors_total`\n- Log: \"Failed to update container resources\" \u2192 indicates reconciliation failure\n\n#### Device Plugin Health Monitoring\n**Mechanism**:\n- Device manager periodically calls `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity()`\n- Expects non-zero capacity for healthy plugin\n- Marks devices unhealthy if plugin reports status=unhealthy\n\n**Risk**: Transient network glitch \u2192 device marked unhealthy \u2192 pods using device evicted \u2192 thrashing\n\n**Mitigation**: Device manager has grace period (default 30s) before marking unhealthy; allows transient recoveries.\n\n### 6.3 Scaling Characteristics\n\n#### Cgroup Hierarchy Depth\n- **Current design**: kubepods \u2192 [qos-class] \u2192 [pod-uid] \u2192 [container-name]\n- **Depth**: 4 levels\n- **Scalability**: Cgroup performance degrades linearly with depth (each level adds cgroup tree traversal)\n- **Impact**: On nodes with 5000+ containers, cgroup operations (limit updates, memory queries) may take 100-500ms\n- **Mitigation**: Monitor cgroup operation latencies; alert if exceeding 100ms\n\n#### Container Count Impact on CPU Manager\n- **State size**: O(n) where n = number of ever-created containers\n- **Reconciliation time**: O(n) per interval (default 5s)\n- **Memory overhead**: ~1KB per container tracking\n- **Scaling limit**: Typically comfortable up to 10,000 containers per node\n\n#### Device Plugin Scalability\n- **Allocation latency**: Synchronous call to device plugin during pod admission\n- **Typical latency**: 10-100ms\n- **Scaling risk**: If device plugin blocks on I/O (network, disk), admission latency grows\n- **Mitigation**: Set timeout on device plugin calls (configurable; default 30s)\n\n### 6.4 Troubleshooting Guide\n\n#### Common Issues\n\n**Issue 1: Pod Pending Indefinitely with \"Insufficient cpu/memory\"**\n- **Check**: Node resource capacity\n  ```bash\n  kubectl describe node <node>\n  # Check \"Capacity\" and \"Allocatable\"\n  ```\n- **Root causes**:\n  1. All CPU reserved for kubelet/system (increase `--system-reserved`, `--kube-reserved`)\n  2. Device allocation exhausted (check device plugin health)\n  3. Topology manager rejects allocation (check logs for \"topology affinity\" errors)\n- **Fix**: Adjust node reservations or reduce pod CPU requests\n\n**Issue 2: Containers Frequently OOM Killed**\n- **Check**: Pod memory requests vs actual usage\n  ```bash\n  kubectl top pod <pod-name>\n  # Compare RSS vs request/limit\n  ```\n- **Root causes**:\n  1. Memory request too low relative to workload\n  2. Memory limit too strict (not accounting for memory fragmentation)\n  3. Node memory underreserved (BestEffort pods evicting guaranteed)\n- **Fix**: Increase memory request/limit; or increase `--system-reserved` to protect system pods\n\n**Issue 3: CPU Affinity Not Applied (Static CPU Manager)**\n- **Check**: Pod QoS and container CPU requests\n  ```bash\n  kubectl get pod <pod> -o yaml | grep -E \"requests|limits|status\"\n  ```\n- **Conditions**:\n  1. Pod must be Guaranteed (Requests==Limits for all containers)\n  2. Container must request >0 CPU\n  3. CPU manager policy must be \"static\"\n- **Verify**:\n  ```bash\n  # Check CPU manager state file\n  cat /var/lib/kubelet/cpu_manager_state\n  # Verify container CPU affinity\n  cgget -n -e cpuset <pod-cgroup-path>\n  ```\n\n**Issue 4: Device Plugin Not Recognized**\n- **Check**: Device plugin socket creation and kubelet logs\n  ```bash\n  # Device plugin should create socket\n  ls -la /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/\n\n  # Kubelet logs should show registration\n  journalctl -u kubelet | grep -i \"device\"\n  ```\n- **Root causes**:\n  1. Plugin socket not created at expected path\n  2. Plugin socket permissions incorrect (not readable by kubelet)\n  3. Plugin `Allocate()` call timeout (takes >30s)\n- **Fix**: Verify plugin socket creation; increase timeout if needed; check plugin logs\n\n#### Debugging Commands\n\n```bash\n# Check CPU affinity on running container\ntaskset -c -p <container-pid>\n\n# Query cgroup limits\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods/<pod-cgroup>/cpuset.cpus\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory/kubepods/<pod-cgroup>/memory.limit_in_bytes\n\n# Verify CPU manager state\ncat /var/lib/kubelet/cpu_manager_state | jq '.policyState'\n\n# Monitor cgroup operations\nstrace -e openat,ioctl -p <kubelet-pid> 2>&1 | grep cgroup | head -50\n\n# Check device plugin status\nls -la /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/kubelet.sock\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directories\n\n### Core Container Manager Files\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | ContainerManager interface definition; shared types (CgroupName, ResourceConfig, NodeConfig) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux implementation; cgroup initialization, manager composition |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows implementation; job object-based resource isolation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | Type definitions for cgroup and pod container managers |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v1 filesystem operations; multiple subsystem hierarchies |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v2 filesystem operations; unified hierarchy |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` | Pre/post-container hooks for resource manager integration |\n\n### QoS and Pod Cgroup Management\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` | Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort cgroup hierarchy management |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` | Per-pod cgroup lifecycle; ensures pod cgroup exists before pod starts |\n\n### Resource Managers\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` | CPU allocation manager; coordinates policy execution |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_static.go` | Static CPU allocation policy; exclusive CPU binding |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_none.go` | No CPU allocation; shared pool only |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/` | CPU allocation state persistence (checkpoint, in-memory) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/` | NUMA-aware memory allocation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/` | Device plugin coordination and allocation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/` | Cross-manager topology hint coordination |\n\n### Integration with Container Runtime and Pod Workers\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go` | Container runtime manager; calls InternalContainerLifecycle hooks |\n| `pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go` | Pod sync orchestration; calls containerManager methods during pod lifecycle |\n| `pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go` | Main kubelet class; owns containerManager instance |\n\n### Testing and Utilities\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/fake_container_manager.go` | Mock for testing |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/testing/mocks.go` | Generated mocks using mockery tool |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go` | Utility functions (cgroup path parsing, cgroup names, etc.) |\n\n### Checkpoints and State Storage\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `${KubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state` | CPU allocation checkpoint (JSON); single source of truth for CPU affinity |\n| `${KubeletRootDir}/memory_manager_state` | Memory allocation checkpoint (if memory manager enabled) |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Summary: Key Architectural Principles\n\n1. **Layered Abstraction**: Container manager abstracts cgroup operations via CgroupManager interface; enables backend switching (systemd vs raw cgroupfs)\n\n2. **Pluggable Resource Managers**: CPU, memory, device, and topology managers are independently configurable; allows customization per workload pattern\n\n3. **State-Driven Reconciliation**: All managers maintain persistent state (checkpoints) and periodically reconcile actual system state; enables recovery from kubelet restart and detection of state drift\n\n4. **Hook-Based Integration**: Container lifecycle hooks (PreStart, PostStop) allow resource managers to finalize allocations after container creation; prevents race conditions\n\n5. **Topology-Aware Coordination**: Topology manager ensures resource alignment across managers (CPU, memory, devices) for optimal NUMA performance\n\n6. **QoS-Based Isolation**: Three-tier QoS hierarchy (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) provides predictable SLAs with flexible resource sharing\n\n7. **Early Validation**: System requirements validated at startup; prevents silent degradation and makes failures obvious\n\n8. **CRI-Based Enforcement**: Final enforcement delegated to container runtime via UpdateContainerResources(); kubelet is coordinator, not enforcer\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe kubelet container manager subsystem provides a sophisticated yet maintainable framework for resource management on Kubernetes nodes. Its design balances operational simplicity (cgroup abstraction, QoS hierarchy) with extensibility (pluggable managers, device plugins, topology hints). Understanding the interaction between pod workers, container runtime, and resource managers is essential for troubleshooting performance issues, tuning for specific workloads, and extending the system to support new resource types.\n",

# Kubelet Container Manager Subsystem Architecture Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### Purpose
The kubelet container manager (CM) subsystem is responsible for managing the lifecycle and resource allocation of containers on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the bridge between the kubelet's pod orchestration logic and the node's resource constraints (CPU, memory, devices), enforcing QoS guarantees and ensuring proper container isolation through cgroups.

### Boundaries
The container manager operates at the **node level**, managing all containers across all pods running on a single machine. It is distinct from:
- **Pod lifecycle management** (handled by pod workers in `pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`)
- **Container runtime integration** (handled by kuberuntime in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`)
- **Image management** (separate subsystem for pulling and caching images)

### Key Dependencies
- **Upstream**: Pod workers (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`) drive container creation requests; node API provides resource specifications
- **Downstream**:
  - Container runtime (`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`) executes actual container operations via CRI (Container Runtime Interface)
  - cAdvisor (`pkg/kubelet/cadvisor/`) provides node capacity and resource metrics
  - cgroups filesystem or systemd interfaces for enforcing resource limits
- **Horizontal**: Device manager, CPU manager, memory manager, topology manager for resource-specific policies

---

## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Splits

### 2.1 ContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go)
The core abstraction defining the container manager contract.

**Primary Responsibilities**:
- `Start()` - Initialize the container manager, validate system requirements, establish cgroup hierarchy
- `Get
